What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Friday, July 28 - 路透新闻

{{20170727T184128.593+0000}}What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Friday, July 28(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT)

The U.S Commerce Department issues its advanced second-quarter gross domestic product estimate, which is likely to have increased 2.6 percent compared with a 1.4 percent rise in the previous quarter. The Commerce Department will also report that advanced core PCE prices for the second quarter are forecast to rise 0.8 percent, but lower than a 2.0 percent rise in the first quarter. (0830/1230) The final reading of University of Michigan Surveys of Consumers Sentiment Index for July is expected to remain unchanged at 93.1 from the previous month. (1000/1400) The Labor Department issues the second quarter Employment Cost Index, which is likely to have gained 0.6 percent. (0830/1230)

Investor focus will be on the performance of Merck & Co Inc's high-profile cancer drug Keytruda as the drugmaker reports second-quarter results amid rising competition in the lung cancer market. Investors will also be looking for comments on the multiple myeloma trials, which were testing Keytruda in combination with Celgene's standard of care treatments, and were placed on clinical hold by the U.S regulator earlier this month. Meanwhile, AbbVie Inc also reports second quarter results that are likely to be helped by increased sales of its flagship drug, Humira. Investors will also look for comment on its cancer drug Imbruvica, which analysts expect to become an important revenue driver for the drugmaker.

Exxon Mobil Corp, the world's largest publicly traded oil producer, is expected to post a second quarter profit. Separately, U.S. oil producer Chevron Corp is also expected to post a second quarter profit.

Baker Hughes reports second quarter results. The world's second-largest oilfield services provider, created by Baker Hughes' merger with GE's oil and gas equipment operations, is expected to report quarterly revenue of $2.34 billion and a loss of 15 cents per share in its maiden quarterly release. Investors will be keen on knowing how the company plans to run its business in an uncertain oil market.

Barclays Plc reports first half earnings, with alleged misdeeds by bank executives past and present threatening to overshadow the lender's financial performance. Chief Executive Jes Staley faces a regulatory probe into his attempts to unmask a whistleblower, while the bank has hit headlines in recent months over the trial of its former CEO and others for conduct during its crisis-era Qatar bailout. From a business point of view investors may focus on whether Barclays repeats its dire first quarter bond trading performance, a problem which U.S. rivals saw continue into the period ended June.

Credit Suisse Group AG reports second quarter results. After raising 4 billion Swiss francs earlier this year to plug a hole in its balance sheet, Tidjane Thiam will give an update on his restructure of Switzerland's second-biggest bank two years into his tenure as CEO. Investors and analysts are keen to see healthy inflows at its core wealth management businesses, an improvement at its global markets trading division - the source of billions of dollars in losses last year - and progress in winding down its "bad bank".

Goodyear Tire & Rubber Co reports second quarter results. The U.S. tire maker is expected to report a drop in profit and revenue due to a decrease in its tire shipments. The company has been struggling with a decline in heavy-duty truck production in the United States as a result of oversupply in the market. The company has also been cutting costs and has hiked tire prices to counter higher raw material costs. Investors will look for updates on its long-term forecasts.

American Airlines Group Inc is expected to report strong second quarter financial results. The No. 1 U.S. airline in its June traffic report raised guidance on closely watched metrics including pre-tax margins and total revenue per available seat mile.

The Federal Reserve Bank of Minneapolis President Neel Kashkari participates in a moderated question-and-answer session before a Woodbury Area/St. Paul Chamber of Commerce event, Oakdale, Minneapolis. (1320/1720)

Canada's Bombardier Inc will report second quarter earnings amid industry speculation that the plane and train maker is poised to form new rail joint ventures with Germany's Siemens AG. Bombardier executives, however, are not expected to discuss recent media reports that the two companies could form separate joint ventures in signaling and rolling stock as early as August. Analysts will be watching for an update on the company's cash flow and whether Bombardier's guidance for 30 to 35 CSeries jet deliveries remains on track for 2017. Statistics Canada may report that the Canadian economy grew by 0.2 percent in May. The report is likely to support analysts' expectations that the economy maintained its momentum in the second quarter after a strong start to the year. (0830/1230)

Brazil's IGP-M price index for July, which includes wholesale and consumer prices, is forecast to fall 0.65 percent. The index had fallen 0.67 percent in June. The country's inflation has plunged as the economy struggles to recover from its worst recession on record. (0700/1100) The unemployment rate is expected to remain unchanged at 13.3 percent in June from the previous month.(0800/1200) Meanwhile, the country is expected to post a budget deficit of 19.25 billion reais in June compared with a deficit of 30.70 billion reais in May.(1000/1400) Chile's manufacturing output is expected to fall 1.1 percent in June from a year earlier. (0900/1300)

Trump'ın dış politika danışmanları arasında huzursuzluk kaynama noktasında  - Reuters (Turkish)

{{20170725T122402.549+0000}}Trump'ın dış politika danışmanları arasında huzursuzluk kaynama noktasında John Walcott

WASHINGTON, 25 Temmuz (Reuters) - ABD Başkanı Donald Trump'ın önde gelen dış politika danışmanları arasında, politika ve bürokrasi ile ilişkilerde uğradıkları yenilgilerin yanı sıra görevlerinde bağımsız olmamanın yarattığı hoşnutsuzluk artıyor.

Yetkililer, dış politikada geleneksel "ABD önderliğini" savunan enternasyonalistler ile "Önce Amerika" yaklaşımını benimseyenler arasındaki çekişmelerin, hükümetteki dış politika ve istihbarat profesyonellerini bezdirdiğini söylüyorlar.

Dışişleri Bakanı Rex Tillerson'un dostlarıyla yaptığı sohbetlerde, "görevde bir yılı doldurursa kendisini talihli sayacağını" söylediği konuşuluyor.

Konuya yakın bir kaynak da Reuters'e "Tillerson kendi bakanlığında özerkliğe, bağımsızlığa ve denetime sahip olamamaktan ve görevini alışıldığı gibi yapamamaktan dolayı çok rahatsız olduğunu söyledi" dedi.

Tillerson'un görevden ayrılmasına ilişkin ise herhangi bir bilgiye sahip olmadığını da söyleyen aynı kaynak "Ancak durum iyiye gitmiyor, hatta bazı açılardan daha da kötüleşiyor" diye konuştu.

Tillerson'un görevden ayrılacağı yolundaki söylentiyi kesin bir dille reddeden sözcüsü R.C. Hammond ise, "Dünyanın Amerikan liderliğine çok acil ihtiyacı var ve Bakan da dikkatini buraya veriyor" dedi.

Suudi Arabistan, Birleşik Arap Emirlikleri, Bahreyn ve Mısır'ın geçen ay Katar'ı terörizmi finanse etmekle suçlayarak uyguladıkları boykot üzerine Tillerson bu ülkelerden ablukayı gevşetmelerini istemiş ve krizi sona erdirme yükümlüğünü her iki tarafa da paylaştırmıştı.

Tillerson'un bu açıklamasından yarım saat sonra ise Trump, Katar'ı önde gelen bir terör destekçisi olmakla suçlayarak, Katar'a uygulanan ambargoyu diğer Arap liderlerle birlikte hazırladıklarını ima eden ifadeler kullanmıştı.

Sözcü Hammond bu gelişmelerin ardından "Hükümet olarak akıl karıştıran sinyaller verdik, ama daha sonra durumu açıklığa kavuşturabildik" demişti.

Bu arada iki istihbarat görevlisi de ulusal güvenlik danışmanı H.R. McMaster'ın Beyaz Saray'da önemli dış politika konularındaki örgütsüzlük ve disiplinsizlikten şikayetçi olduğunu söylediler.

Kıdemli ulusal güvenlik yetkilileri, McMaster'in, yardımcısı Rusya direktörü Fiona Hill'in de katıldığı bir tutumla, Rusya Devlet Başkanı Vladimir Putin'e karşı sert tavır alınması yönündeki tavsiyesinin dikkate alınmamasından dolayı kırgın olduğunu söylüyorlar.

Trump, ABD istihbarat kurumlarının Rusya'nın 2016 başkanlık seçimine rakibi Hillary Clinton aleyhinde müdahale ettiği yolundaki görüşlerini dikkate almıyor.

Emekli bir korgeneral olan McMaster'ın Afganistan'da Taliban'la mücadele için daha çok asker gönderilmesi konusunun bitmek bilmeyen tartışmalarla uzamasından da rahatsız olduğu söyleniyor.

Dışişleri Bakanı olmadan önce Exxon Mobil Corp'un CEO'su olan Tillerson, yeni göreviyle eskisini karşılaştırması istendiğinde geçen ay şöyle konuşmuştu:

"(Exxon Mobil'de) son kararı veren bendim. Bu her zaman işleri kolaylaştırır, ne bekleyebileceğimi bilirdim ve çok eskiye dayanan disiplinli karar verme süreçlerimiz vardı. ABD hükümetinde ise böyle nitelikler yok."

Haberin orijinali için tıklayınız: [nL1N1KG00Q] ÖNEMLİ: Bu haber, linkleri yukarıda belirtilen haber ya da haberlerden derlenmiştir. Tam çevrilmiş metin olmayabilir

(Haberi çeviren Ayşe Sarıoğlu; Redaksiyon Gülsen Solaker) ((Mehmet.Dinar@thomsonreuters.com; +90 312 292 7000;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

RPT-After false dawn, Big Oil to double down on cost cuts - Reuters News

{{20170724T060002.046+0000}}RPT-After false dawn, Big Oil to double down on cost cuts(Repeats, adds link to graphic dividend yield)

* Q2 income set to double y/y as cost cuts pay off

* Profits to drop on quarter after oil price recovery stalls

* GRAPHIC: Oil companies dividend yield http://tmsnrt.rs/2ui9dZ8

* GRAPHIC: Oil companies performance http://reut.rs/2twyZvW

* GRAPHIC: Oil majors gearing http://reut.rs/2t1h64h

By Ron Bousso

LONDON, July 21 (Reuters) - After a brief respite at the start of the year, the world's top oil and gas companies are set to double down on cost cutting as a recovery in crude prices after a three-year slump falters.

Corporate hopes were raised by a deal between members of the Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries and other non-OPEC producers to cut production, which lifted oil prices above $58 a barrel in January, after they had slid to as low as $27 in 2016.

But Brent crude prices have since slipped back below $50 and banks have lowered price forecasts, amid surging output from the United States and other nations not bound by the global oil pact.

Investors are again focussing on the ability of top oil firms such as Exxon Mobil , Royal Dutch Shell and Total to live within their means and eke out profits when oil has failed to recover, as hoped, to $60.

The majors, often dubbed Big Oil, have already been through tough spending cuts since a collapse in crude prices since mid-2014 from above $100. They have shed thousands of jobs, scrapped projects, sold assets and squeezed service costs.

The painstaking effort has paid off.

Net income for Exxon, Chevron , Shell, BP , Total, Eni and Statoil is set to double on average in the quarter ending June 30 from a year earlier, even though oil prices are back as similar levels, according to analyst estimates compiled by Reuters.

By early 2017, management teams said their operations in 2017 would cover spending and dividend payouts at $60 a barrel, although for many firms this included using scrip programmes, when investors can opt for dividend payouts in shares not cash.

"MORE OF THE SAME"

But earlier savings may not now be enough, with Brent crude averaging below $50 in the second quarter and forecasts that the 2017 average will be $54. [O/POLL]

While net income for Q2 may climb year-on-year, the quarter-on-quarter picture is different. Compared to the first three months of the year, the second quarter will see net income fall by about 20 percent, according to analyst estimates.

"Given where oil prices are, 2017 is still a year of transition for these companies, and that is not necessarily supportive for investment," said Jason Kenney, head of pan-European oil and gas equity research at Banco Santander.

"The sector needs to continue doing more of the same," he said, referring to the ongoing need to reduce costs.

Dividend yield, the ratio between a firm's dividend payout and share price, has risen in recent weeks to near recent highs as share prices have slipped, underscoring investor concerns.

Shell, Statoil and Total kick off the Q2 earnings reports on Thursday, followed by Exxon and Chevron on Friday. BP reports on Aug. 1.

Majors were targetting break even at $55 a barrel and could further cut spending by delaying investments, simplifying offshore and other project designs and selling assets, Kenney said.

About two thirds of the industry's capital expenditure went to new projects, with the rest used to maintain existing output, Kenney added.

"OFF LIFE SUPPORT"

Company boards have taken different approaches to deal with the bumpy oil price recovery.

Exxon and Chevron have invested in U.S. shale oil in recent months, seeking to benefit from the relatively low development cost and the short time it takes to extract commercial oil.

Across the Atlantic, Shell, BP and Total have focussed more heavily on cutting costs of large, deepwater oil and gas projects to compete with the low-cost shale. [nL8N1JG4D4]

Analysts have rewarded some firms for their ongoing savings. Total holds 18 "strong buy" or "buy" recommendations, while Chevron has 17, among analysts polled by Reuters. Shell has 16.

Exxon holds the lowest number of "buy" recommendations at 8. Its high share price to earnings (P/E) ratio and a weaker production growth outlook make it less attractive, HSBC said.

Exxon shares are trading at a P/E ratio of 16.9, compared with Shell's 11.9 and BP's 10.3.

Oil majors have underperformed so far this year relative to the broader stock market . For some, that makes current valuations attractive. (See graphic: http://reut.rs/2twyZvW)

"The fundamental environment is looking quite good because this is an environment where (companies) can cut costs and reduce headcount and they don't have to develop anything," said Jonathan Waghorn, co-manager of the energy fund at Guinness Asset Management, which holds shares in Shell, BP, Total and Chevron. "They are off life support at $55 a barrel."

^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^> (Reporting by Ron Bousso; Editing by Edmund Blair) ((ron.bousso@thomsonreuters.com; +44)(0)(2075422161; Reuters Messaging: ron.bousso.reuters.com@reuters.net))

{{20170723T064229.333+0000}}Saudi refinery operations not affected by transformer fire KHOBAR, Saudi Arabia, July 23 (Reuters) - The Saudi Aramco Mobile Refinery (SAMREF) at Yanbu is operating normally after a fire hit a power transformer at the gate of the facility on Saturday, a spokesman for a Saudi government body was quoted as saying on the state news agency.

Operations are ongoing and have not been affected by the incident, which happened due to hot weather, Abdulrahman Al-Abdulqader, the spokesman for the Royal Commission for Jubail and Yanbu, which manages and operates industrial cities in Saudi Arabia. The fire broke out at 21:22 local time, according to the spokesman.

SAMREF is a joint venture between Saudi Aramco and U.S. Exxon Mobil which operates the 400,000 barrel per day (bpd) crude oil refinery in Yanbu on the Red Sea coast of Saudi Arabia.

A SAMREF spokesman could not be immediately reached for comment.

(Editing by Jane Merriman) ((Reem.Shamseddine@thomsonreuters.com; +966503335202; Reuters Messaging: reem.shamseddine.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, July 24 - 路透新闻

{{20170721T200342.534+0000}}What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, July 24(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT.)

WEEKAHEAD

Investors, next week, will focus on the Federal Reserve's two-day policy meeting that will begin on Tuesday. Expectations that the U.S. central bank will leave key overnight borrowing costs unchanged partly fed the decline in short-term interest rate volatility. Markets will work through another spate of economic figures that include gross domestic product, data on labor costs, durable goods figures, consumer confidence index, single-family home prices and data on mortgage applications. On Friday, the gross domestic product for the second quarter is expected to have increased at a 2.6 percent annual rate. On the same day, the Employment Cost Index is likely to have gained 0.6 percent in the second quarter. On Tuesday, the S&P CoreLogic Case-Shiller composite index of 20 metropolitan areas, which measures U.S. single-family home prices, is expected to have increased 5.8 percent in May. In a separate report on the same day, the U.S. Conference Board is expected to show a drop in its consumer confidence index. The index is expected to have slipped to a reading of 116.5 in July, from 118.9 in June. The Mortgage Bankers Association's weekly index for mortgage applications is on the tap for Wednesday. On Thursday, overall orders for durable goods, items ranging from toasters to aircraft that are meant to last three years or more, are expected to have increased 2.6 percent in June.

A slew of Dow 30 companies, including chemicals conglomerate DuPont, industrial conglomerate United Technologies Corp, Scotch tape and Post-it notes maker 3M Co, Exxon Mobil Corp, Chevron and the heavy machinery manufacturer Caterpillar Inc are scheduled to report results next week. Exxon Mobil is expected to post profit in the second quarter on Friday. Chevron also reports its second-quarter results on the same day. DuPont is expected to report a rise in second-quarter profit on Tuesday, due to higher demand for seeds. As Dow and DuPont are nearing the completion of their deal, investors will keep an eye out for leadership of the combined company. 3M Co is also expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second-quarter on the same day, led by higher sales in its industrials unit, which makes industrial tapes and adhesives, and caters to automotive, aerospace, electronics and packaging industries. Meanwhile, Caterpillar is expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter on Tuesday, helped by improving demand in the construction and energy industries. Separately, when United Technologies will post its second-quarter results on Tuesday, investors will be looking for updates on solving problems with its Pratt & Whitney engines, which have delayed delivery of some Airbus planes.

Amazon.com Inc is expected to report a rise in quarterly revenue on Thursday, helped by growth in its retail and cloud computing businesses. Investors will look for more details on Amazon's surprise $13.7 billion deal to buy upscale grocer Whole Foods Market, which could upend the already struggling U.S. retail industry. Investors will also focus on Amazon's current-quarter forecast, which will include sales from its annual Prime day shopping event that expanded to China, India and Mexico this year.

Facebook Inc reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. The social media giant is expected to post a rise in profit and revenue driven by its fast-growing mobile ad business. Facebook is searching for new types of advertising features to supplement its main revenue streams that it expects to cool off this year. Any update on its plans to beef up its features would be interesting.

On Tuesday, General Motors releases its second-quarter results, amid investor concern about declining demand in the United States. The company has already flagged higher-than-projected costs related to the sale of Opel to PSA. Ford Motor Co reports second-quarter results on Wednesday, the first since new CEO Jim Hackett took charge. He could elaborate on his plans to reevaluate Ford operations and speed decisions.

MasterCard Inc, the world's second-biggest payments processor is expected to report a rise in second-quarter profit on Thursday, with higher cross-border volumes growth. However, costs are expected to rise due to the two acquisitions it made in Q1, VocaLink and NuData Security. Investors will also look for any update on the card company's progress to start operations in China.

Eli Lilly & Co is likely to report higher second-quarter earnings on Tuesday, according to Thomson Reuters data, helped by strong sales of its diabetes treatments. Biogen Inc is also expected to report its second-quarter results before the bell on the same day. Investors will focus on the performance of Biogen's pricey new spinal muscular atrophy drug, Spinraza, amid slowing sales of its best-selling multiple sclerosis (MS) treatment Tecfidera. Meanwhile, Merck & Co. Inc will report its second-quarter results on Friday. Investor focus will be on the performance of the company's high-profile cancer drug Keytruda as the drugmaker reports second-quarter results amid rising competition in the lung cancer market. AbbVie Inc will also report second-quarter results on the same day, that is likely to be helped by increased sales of its flagship drug, Humira. Investors will also look for comment on its cancer drug Imbruvica, which analysts expect to become an important revenue driver for the drugmaker. Celgene Corp's second-quarter results scheduled for release on Thursday, are likely to be helped by sales of its blockbuster cancer drug, Revlimid, whose sales have slowed in the past few quarters.

Health insurer Anthem Inc reports second-quarter results before the bell on Wednesday in the wake of the failed Republican effort to overhaul or repeal Obamacare. Investors will look for comments from Anthem, which sells Blue Cross Blue Shield plans in 14 states, about the state of the health insurance industry. Mid-cap health insurer Centene Corp, which primarily focuses on government-sponsored plans, is set to report higher second-quarter earnings on Tuesday, due to acquisitions and increased membership. Investors will focus on how the health insurer keeps its medicaid business profitable amid changing dynamics of the health insurance industry under President Donald Trump's administration.

Boston Scientific Corp reports second-quarter results on Thursday. Investors will likely focus on Boston Scientific's heart device, Lotus valve system's performance in comparison to Medtronic Plc's CoreValve TAVI system. Analysts expect the company to outperform its large-cap med device peers as the company's robust pipeline products will contribute meaningfully to revenue.

AT&T is expected to post a fall in second-quarter revenue on Tuesday, as the largest U.S. TV provider looks to close its $85.4 billion acquisition of Time Warner. According to sources, AT&T will run its wireless and DirecTV satellite television businesses separately from Time Warner's media assets, analysts will be looking out for any commentary regarding this. On the wireless front, AT&T is likely to struggle to keep its subscribers amid stiff competition. Meanwhile, Verizon Communications Inc reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The No. 1 U.S. wireless carrier is expected to report its fifth straight quarter of revenue declines. The company, which has been facing stiff competition from smaller rivals such as T-Mobile and Sprint, are likely to lose customers to other players in the market.

Texas Instruments Inc reports second-quarter results on Tuesday. The chipmaker is expected to post a rise in quarterly revenue, helped by demand for analog and embedded chip products from the automotive and industrial markets.

Twitter Inc reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The microblogging service is expected to report its second fall in revenue in its latest quarter since its debut. Chief Executive Jack Dorsey, whose leadership has been questioned amidst stagnating user growth, is looking to shake things up for the company to cope with stiff competition from Facebook and Snapchat. However, Twitter reported better-than-expected growth in its monthly active users last quarter and any sign of that momentum continuing will be closely monitored as the company looks to woo users with a revamped interface and wider offerings.

Coca-Cola Co is expected to report second-quarter results on Wednesday. Coca-Cola is looking to cut costs, mainly by reducing 1,200 jobs, and invest in growing its non-carbonated beverage business amid falling demand for fizzy drinks globally. The company in April forecast a smaller decline in 2017 adjusted profit than it had previously expected.

McDonald's Corp is expected to report its second-quarter results on Tuesday. The company is seeking to reverse years of traffic declines at its U.S. restaurants with the introduction of cooked-to-order Quarter Pounders made from fresh beef, higher-end signature crafted sandwiches and mobile and kiosk ordering, while also testing home delivery. Chipotle Mexican Grill Inc also reports second-quarter results on the same day. Chipotle's fragile recovery from a string of food safety lapses in 2015 likely will overshadow Tuesday's quarterly financial report, which lands just days after the chain briefly closed a Virginia restaurant due to norovirus and a video of mice in a Dallas restaurant went viral.

Hershey Co reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. The Hershey Kisses and Cadbury chocolates maker's second-quarter sales is expected to grow as the company has been launching a flurry of new products to keep up with demand from snack-loving consumers in the United States, its home turf. The company has also been keeping a tight lid on costs to help mitigate loss from its China business.

General Dynamics Corp, the maker of Gulfstream jets, is expected to report higher revenue for the second quarter on Wednesday, helped by stable demand for its business jets in North America. Investors will look for an update on full-year financial forecast. U.S. weapons maker Northrop Grumman Corp is also expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter on Wednesday, helped by higher sales in its aerospace unit, which makes parts for F-35 fighter jets, drones and spacecraft. Investors will look for an update on full-year financial forecast. Raytheon Co, the maker of Tomahawk missiles, is expected to report higher revenue in the second quarter on Thursday, as it sees increased demand for its products fueled by a pro-defense Trump administration and U.S. allies. Investors will look for an update on 2017 financial forecast. D.R. Horton Inc, the No.1 U.S. homebuilder is expected to report a rise in fourth-quarter revenue and profit on Wednesday, helped by higher home sales. An improving job market has supported U.S. housing demand but homebuilders continue to face land and labor shortages. Investors will look for the company's financial forecast and details on its pending deal with real estate developer Forestar Group Inc. On Tuesday, PulteGroup Inc, the third biggest U.S. homebuilder is expected to post increases in second-quarter profit and revenue as strong housing demand drives higher home sales. Investors will look for the details on the company's financial forecast.

Nasdaq, the transatlantic exchange operator, will report its second-quarter earnings on Wednesday. Net income is expected to rise, helped by higher trading revenue. Expenses are expected to fall. Nasdaq also bought Canadian stock trading venue CXC and news distribution company Marketwired last year and will continue to benefit from the acquisition. The exchange industry is in the midst of a wave of consolidation as companies seek to move more trading onto fewer technology platforms to boost profit margins.

The New York Times Co reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The newspaper publisher is expected to swing to a quarterly profit from a year-earlier loss, as it benefits from higher digital subscriptions. The Times has been investing in marketing to sign up more digital subscribers even as it cuts costs through restructuring that job cuts. It offered buyouts to some of its newsroom employees in May in an effort to streamline editing and production systems.

Citigroup holds its first day-long conference for investors since 2008 on Tuesday. Nearly a decade after Citigroup suspended "Investor Day" conferences during the financial crisis, bank executives say they are ready to again meet in an auditorium with big investors and securities analysts to talk about their strategy to boost shareholder returns. The conference comes after Chief Executive Mike Corbat failed to meet performance targets that he set in 2013 shortly after directors fired the previous CEO and put Corbat in charge.

Canada's second-largest oil and gas producer, Suncor Energy Inc, reports second-quarter earnings on Wednesday. Suncor has endured lower-than-expected oil prices and problems at the Syncrude oil sands plant, in which it is the majority owner. Investors will look for updates to Suncor's strategy and progress reports on Syncrude and the company's new Fort Hills and Hebron projects.

Alaska Air Group reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. Analysts expect Alaska Air's results to improve from the preceding quarter's steep earnings drop. The West Coast airline in December bought rival Virgin America in a $2.6 billion deal to become the fifth-largest U.S. carrier.

The main economic event in Canada next week will be monthly gross domestic product for May, released on Friday. The report will likely support analysts' expectations that the economy maintained its momentum in the second quarter after a strong start to the year. Stronger-than-expected growth could also underscore expectations that the Bank of Canada will hike interest rates again in the coming months.

ON MONDAY

Google's parent company, Alphabet Inc, is expected to report increases in second-quarter profit and revenue, helped by strong advertising sales on mobile devices and for video content. The company's cloud computing business has long trailed those of Amazon.com Inc and Microsoft Corp, although it has managed to win some major deals. Investors will look for updates on Google's plan to beef up its cloud business, as its dependence on search has been a worry.

Six ministers from OPEC and non-OPEC nations Kuwait, Venezuela, Algeria, Saudi Arabia, Russia and Oman as well as OPEC's secretary general will meet in St Petersburg, Russia to discuss the current situation in the oil market. Traders predicted prices would hold near current levels ahead of Monday's meeting between key OPEC and non-OPEC producers in St. Petersburg. The market has been watching reports that Saudi Arabia, the world's largest crude producer, is considering an additional supply cut to bring markets into balance.

The Markit U.S Manufacturing Purchasing Managers' Index (PMI) for July is expected to come in at 52.1 compared with 52.0 in the previous month. Markit services PMI for July is expected at 54.3. (0945/1345) The National Association of Realtors is likely to say that existing home sales dropped to 5.57 million units in June. U.S. home resales unexpectedly rose in May to 5.62 million units. (1000/1400)

Hasbro Inc, the No.2 U.S. toymaker, is expected to post second-quarter revenue above analysts' estimates, helped by higher shipments of toys based on the "Transformers: The Last Knight" and "Spider-Man: Homecoming" movies.

Halliburton Co is expected to report a profit in the second quarter, compared to a year-ago loss, helped by increased demand for its pressure pumping and well-construction services. U.S. shale producers have been putting more rigs to work, buoyed by oil prices that are hovering close to $50. Investors will see whether Halliburton can keep up the optimistic tone set by market leader Schlumberger.

A newly established U.S.-UK trade and investment working group will hold its first meeting in Washington to scope out plans for a potential free trade agreement between the two countries after Brexit. The meeting will take place in Washington at the U.S. Trade Representative's office and will include Liam Fox, the UK secretary for international trade, and Donald Trump's trade czar Robert Lighthizer.

Statistics Canada is expected to show a slower rise in Canadian wholesale trade for May. Canadian wholesale trade is expected to rise 0.5 percent in May after a 1.0 percent gain in April. (0830/1230)

After false dawn, Big Oil to double down on cost cuts - Reuters News

{{20170721T142838.851+0000}}After false dawn, Big Oil to double down on cost cuts* Q2 income set to double y/y as cost cuts pay off

* Profits to drop on quarter after oil price recovery stalls

* GRAPHIC: Oil companies performance http://reut.rs/2twyZvW

* GRAPHIC: Oil majors gearing http://reut.rs/2t1h64h

By Ron Bousso

LONDON, July 21 (Reuters) - After a brief respite at the start of the year, the world's top oil and gas companies are set to double down on cost cutting as a recovery in crude prices after a three-year slump falters.

Corporate hopes were raised by a deal between members of the Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries and other non-OPEC producers to cut production, which lifted oil prices above $58 a barrel in January, after they had slid to as low as $27 in 2016.

But Brent crude prices have since slipped back below $50 and banks have lowered price forecasts, amid surging output from the United States and other nations not bound by the global oil pact.

Investors are again focussing on the ability of top oil firms such as Exxon Mobil , Royal Dutch Shell and Total to live within their means and eke out profits when oil has failed to recover, as hoped, to $60.

The majors, often dubbed Big Oil, have already been through tough spending cuts since a collapse in crude prices since mid-2014 from above $100. They have shed thousands of jobs, scrapped projects, sold assets and squeezed service costs.

The painstaking effort has paid off.

Net income for Exxon, Chevron , Shell, BP , Total, Eni and Statoil is set to double on average in the quarter ending June 30 from a year earlier, even though oil prices are back as similar levels, according to analyst estimates compiled by Reuters.

By early 2017, management teams said their operations in 2017 would cover spending and dividend payouts at $60 a barrel, although for many firms this included using scrip programmes, when investors can opt for dividend payouts in shares not cash.

"MORE OF THE SAME"

But earlier savings may not now be enough, with Brent crude averaging below $50 in the second quarter and forecasts that the 2017 average will be $54. [O/POLL]

While net income for Q2 may climb year-on-year, the quarter-on-quarter picture is different. Compared to the first three months of the year, the second quarter will see net income fall by about 20 percent, according to analyst estimates.

"Given where oil prices are, 2017 is still a year of transition for these companies, and that is not necessarily supportive for investment," said Jason Kenney, head of pan-European oil and gas equity research at Banco Santander.

"The sector needs to continue doing more of the same," he said, referring to the ongoing need to reduce costs.

Dividend yield, the ratio between a firm's dividend payout and share price, has risen in recent weeks to near recent highs as share prices have slipped, underscoring investor concerns.

Shell, Statoil and Total kick off the Q2 earnings reports on Thursday, followed by Exxon and Chevron on Friday. BP reports on Aug. 1.

Majors were targetting break even at $55 a barrel and could further cut spending by delaying investments, simplifying offshore and other project designs and selling assets, Kenney said.

About two thirds of the industry's capital expenditure went to new projects, with the rest used to maintain existing output, Kenney added.

"OFF LIFE SUPPORT"

Company boards have taken different approaches to deal with the bumpy oil price recovery.

Exxon and Chevron have invested in U.S. shale oil in recent months, seeking to benefit from the relatively low development cost and the short time it takes to extract commercial oil.

Across the Atlantic, Shell, BP and Total have focussed more heavily on cutting costs of large, deepwater oil and gas projects to compete with the low-cost shale. [nL8N1JG4D4]

Analysts have rewarded some firms for their ongoing savings. Total holds 18 "strong buy" or "buy" recommendations, while Chevron has 17, among analysts polled by Reuters. Shell has 16.

Exxon holds the lowest number of "buy" recommendations at 8. Its high share price to earnings (P/E) ratio and a weaker production growth outlook make it less attractive, HSBC said.

Exxon shares are trading at a P/E ratio of 16.9, compared with Shell's 11.9 and BP's 10.3.

Oil majors have underperformed so far this year relative to the broader stock market . For some, that makes current valuations attractive. (See graphic: http://reut.rs/2twyZvW)

"The fundamental environment is looking quite good because this is an environment where (companies) can cut costs and reduce headcount and they don't have to develop anything," said Jonathan Waghorn, co-manager of the energy fund at Guinness Asset Management, which holds shares in Shell, BP, Total and Chevron. "They are off life support at $55 a barrel."

FOKUS 1-US-Ölfeldausrüster Schlumberger will russischen Rivalen - Reuters (German)

{{20170721T122343.060+0000}}FOKUS 1-US-Ölfeldausrüster Schlumberger will russischen Rivalen* Schlumberger bietet für Eurasia Drilling

* Russische Wettbewerbshüter müssen noch zustimmen

* Schlumberger profitiert derzeit von US-Schieferölboom

(Neu: Schlumberger-Geschäftszahlen)

Moskau/Bangalore, 21. Jul (Reuters) - Ein halbes Jahr nach dem Regierungswechsel in den USA unternimmt der Ölfeldausrüster Schlumberger einen zweiten Anlauf zur Übernahme des russischen Branchenführers Eurasia Drilling Co (EDC). Dieser gab am Freitag die Veräußerung einer Mehrheitsbeteiligung von 51 Prozent an den Weltmarktprimus bekannt. Kommt der Deal zustande, wäre es der erste Zukauf eines amerikanischen Konzerns in der Branche auf dem russischen Markt seit der Verhängung von Sanktionen gegen Russland im Zuge der Ukraine-Krise im Jahr 2014.

EDC-Chef Alexander Djaparidse betonte die jahrelangen Geschäftsverbindungen mit dem US-Konzern und erklärte: "Ich heiße Schlumberger als unseren neuen Mehrheitsaktionär herzlich willkommen." Allerdings steht die Zustimmung der russischen Behörden noch aus. Ein Kreml-Sprecher lehnte eine Aussage dazu ab, ob Russland inzwischen mit Wohlwollen auf den US-Investor blickt. Schlumbergers erster Versuch im Jahr 2015 war daran gescheitert, dass die zuständige Behörde ihre Zustimmung mehrfach verschob. Damals wollte der US-Konzern knapp 46 Prozent der EDC-Anteile für 1,7 Milliarden Dollar kaufen.

Inzwischen ist aber der frühere Ölmanager Rex Tillerson US-Außenminister. In dieser Position ist der ehemalige Chef von Exxon Mobil mit dafür zuständig, Entscheidungen über Sanktionen zu treffen. Er gilt als russlandfreundlich und hat wiederholt die gegen das Land verhängten Strafmaßnahmen kritisiert.[nL5N1E74LZ][nL5N1KC0BT]

Zuletzt hatte der US-Senat neue Sanktionen gegen Russland beschlossen, was in der Energiebranche für einen Aufschrei sorgte. Warnungen vor eklatanten Auswirkungen auf die Öl- und Gasversorgung wurden laut.[nL5N1KA5HO] Um Gesetzeskraft zu erlangen, muss die Vorlage allerdings noch das Repräsentantenhaus passieren und von US-Präsident Donald Trump unterzeichnet werden.[nL8N1JC1VV] Für Trump ist das Thema Russland zu einer schweren Hypothek geworden, die seine bisherige Amtszeit belastet. Ein Sonderermittler und Parlamentsausschüsse untersuchen, ob es unzulässige Absprachen zwischen Trumps Wahlkampfteam und der Regierung in Moskau gab.[nL5N1KB1YP]

Für westliche Konzerne ist das Russland-Geschäft deswegen interessant, weil die dortigen Ölfirmen trotz der gesunkenen Preise an ihren Investitionen festhalten. Schlumberger profitierte zuletzt insbesondere vom Schieferölboom in den USA. Der Umsatz stieg im abgelaufenen Quartal um 4,2 Prozent auf 7,46 Milliarden Dollar, der Verlust reduzierte sich kräftig auf 74 Millionen Dollar nach 2,16 Milliarden Dollar vor einem Jahr.

Asia-Pacific Crude-Trading for Australian heavy sweet grades stays brisk - 路透新闻

{{20170721T102631.884+0000}}Asia-Pacific Crude-Trading for Australian heavy sweet grades stays briskSINGAPORE, July 21 (Reuters) - Trading for September-loading Australian heavy sweet crude remained brisk with more details about deals emerging on Friday.

AUSTRALIA

*PYRENEES: Both September-loading Pyrenees cargoes have traded, with BHP Billiton likely to have sold its end-September cargo this week, traders said. Details on the buyers were not immediately known but the cargoes were likely purchased by Chinese participants, they added.

*VAN GOGH: Quadrant sold its September-October cross-month cargo of the heavy sweet crude to Gunvor at around $1.10 per barrel to dated Brent.

*VINCENT: A mid-September cargo of the grade marketed by Mitsui remains on offer and is the last available September-loading Australian heavy sweet cargo in the market.

TENDERS

*THAILAND: Results of the IRPC sweet crude import tender have yet to emerge as the validity for offers expires on Friday.

*MALAYSIA: Petronas is likely to award its September-loading Muda condensate sell tender at a premium higher than August levels of mid-$1.00 per barrel premium to dated Brent, sources with knowledge of the tender said. Validity for bids expire on Friday.

REFINING MARGINS

*Singapore refining margins to Dubai crude , which is Asia's key indicator of refinery profitability, rose to $7.85 per barrel on July 20, the highest since November 29, the day before OPEC-led output cuts were put in place. [nL3N1KC27V]

CHINA

*PetroChina's 260,000-barrel-per-day greenfield refinery in southwestern Yunnan province is due to receive its first supply of sour crude this month, according to shipping data on Thomson Reuters Eikon. [nL3N1KC30O]

BRENT-DUBAI EFS

*Brent's premium to Dubai swaps was at $0.88 per barrel, up 1 cent for September.

REFINED PRODUCTS

*South Korea is in the process of easing blending restrictions at its oil storage terminals as the world's No. 5 crude importer bolsters an effort to become a North Asia trading hub. [nL3N1KC2QO]

*The U.S. gasoline surplus has disappeared thanks to a sharp drop in prices which has caused imports from Europe to slow and exports to Latin America and other markets to accelerate since the start of June. [nL5N1KB5FP]

MARKET NEWS

*Russia's top oil producer Rosneft is negotiating to swap its collateral in Venezuelan-owned, U.S.-based refiner Citgo for oilfield stakes and a fuel supply deal - a move to avoid complications from U.S. sanctions, two sources with knowledge of the negotiations told Reuters. [nL1N1KB28X]

*Exxon Mobil Corp sued the U.S. government on Thursday, blasting as "unlawful" and "capricious" a $2 million fine levied against it for a three-year-old oil joint venture with Russia's Rosneft. [nL1N1KB0RC]

*Saudi Aramco's Manifa oilfield, one of its largest, is producing and has not been affected by any technical issue, an industry source told Reuters on Thursday. [nL5N1KB6G7]

OPEC, NON-OPEC NEWS

*The United Arab Emirates Energy Minister Suhail bin Mohammed al-Mazroui said on Friday he hopes that global supplies will start tightening in the second half of the year when demand picks up. [nL3N1KC2R3]

WDHLG-FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson - Reuters (German)

{{20170721T043203.671+0000}}WDHLG-FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson(Wiederholung vom Vorabend)

* US-Regierung verhängt Strafe wegen Sanktionsverstößen

* Geschäfte wurden 2014 unter heutigem Außenminister getätigt

* Exxon wehrt sich juristisch gegen die Entscheidung - "Unfair"

Washington/Houston, 20. Jul (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil ist wegen Russland-Geschäften zu Zeiten von US-Außenminister Rex Tillerson als Chef des Ölmultis ins Visier der heimischen Behörden geraten. Das US-Finanzministerium verhängte eine Strafe von zwei Millionen Dollar wegen Sanktionsverstößen vor gut drei Jahren. Exxon habe damals die Vorschriften "rücksichtlos missachtet", erklärte das Ministerium am Donnerstag in einer ungewöhnlich ausführlichen Stellungnahme. Konkret wird Exxon vorgeworfen, dass führende Manager im Mai 2014 Vereinbarungen über Öl- und Gasprojekte zusammen mit dem Präsidenten des russischen Konkurrenten Rosneft, Igor Setschin, unterzeichneten - wenige Wochen, nachdem die USA wegen des Ukraine-Konflikts Sanktionen gegen Russland verhängt hatten.

Die US-Regierung hatte Setschin damals wegen seiner engen Verbindung zum russischen Präsidenten Wladimir Putin auf eine schwarzen Liste gesetzt. Die Sanktionen verbieten es in den USA Ansässigen, Geschäfte mit Personen auf dieser Liste zu tätigen. Die nun verhängte Strafe resultiert aus einer Untersuchung jener Vereinbarungen, die Exxon-Manager damals mit Setschin getroffen hatten. Exxon geht juristisch gegen die Strafe vor und bezeichnete die Entscheidung als "grundlegend unfair".

Tillerson hatte Exxon zehn Jahre lang geleitet, bevor er unter US-Präsident Donald Trump zum Außenminister ernannt wurde. In dieser Position ist er mit dafür zuständig, Entscheidungen über Sanktionen zu treffen. Er gilt als russlandfreundlich und hat wiederholt die gegen das Land verhängten Strafmaßnahmen kritisiert. Daran war auch ein Plan für ein Exxon-Rosneft-Gemeinschaftsunternehmen gescheitert. Rosneft-Chef Setschin bezeichnete Tillerson einmal als Freund, mit dem er gerne mal die Vereinigten Staaten auf dem Motorrad durchqueren wolle.[nL5N1E74LZ]

(Reporter: Yeganeh Torbati und Ernest Scheyder; geschrieben von Elke Ahlswede; redigiert von Birgit Mittwollen; Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1236 oder 030-2888 5168) ((elke.ahlswede@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1732; Reuters Messaging: Elke.Ahlswede.reuters.com@reuters.net www.reuters.de www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

ПОВТОР-Минфин США оштрафовал Exxon Mobil на $2 млн за дела с Сечиным - Reuters (Russian)

{{20170721T040001.550+0000}}ПОВТОР-Минфин США оштрафовал Exxon Mobil на $2 млн за дела с СечинымВАШИНГТОН, 20 июл (Рейтер) - Министерство финансов США в четверг оштрафовало американский нефтяной концерн Exxon Mobil Corp и несколько его "дочек" на $2 миллиона за нарушение в мае 2014 года санкций против Игоря Сечина - главы крупнейшей нефтяной компании России Роснефть .

Пресс-секретарь Роснефти Михаил Леонтьев сказал, что не видит связи между этим событием и дальнейшим сотрудничеством Роснефти с Exxon.

Управление по контролю за иностранными активами Минфина США обнаружило, что Exxon Mobil добровольно не сообщила о нарушениях, и пришло к выводу, что "эти нарушения представляют собой вопиющий случай", говорится в сообщении, опубликованном на сайте ведомства (http://bit.ly/2vnvQf2).

Главы американских "дочек" нефтяного гиганта имели дело с теми, "чья собственность и имущественные интересы были заблокированы, в частности, подписав восемь юридических документов, связанных с нефтегазовыми проектами в России, с Игорем Сечиным, главой ОАО Роснефть" и еще одним лицом, попавшим под санкции, сообщил Минфин США.

Роснефть говорит, что американский регулятор не мог не знать о подписании документов в 2014 году.

"Три года документы находились в абсолютном доступе, и мы исключаем возможность, что OFAC про это не знал. Зная, как Exxon работает во всех вопросах с американскими санкциями, мы исключаем возможность, что Exxon не получил исчерпывающих для него разъяснений, пояснений и разрешенй от этого американского регулятора и его санкционных юристов", - сказал Леонтьев по телефону Рейтер.

UPDATE 3-Exxon sues U.S. over fine levied for Russia deal under Tillerson - Reuters News

{{20170720T230108.805+0000}}UPDATE 3-Exxon sues U.S. over fine levied for Russia deal under Tillerson(Recasts, adds material from lawsuit)

By Yeganeh Torbati and Ernest Scheyder

WASHINGTON/HOUSTON, July 20 (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil Corp sued the U.S. government on Thursday, blasting as "unlawful" and "capricious" a $2 million fine levied against it for a three-year-old oil joint venture with Russia's Rosneft .

The U.S. Treasury Department on Thursday morning slapped the world's largest publicly traded oil producer with the fine for "reckless disregard" of U.S. sanctions in dealings with Russia in 2014 when Secretary of State Rex Tillerson was Exxon's chief executive.

The lawsuit and the Treasury's unusually detailed statement on Exxon's conduct represented an extraordinary confrontation between a major American company and the U.S. government, made all the more striking because Exxon's former CEO is now in President Donald Trump's Cabinet.

Exxon took the government to court despite the fact that the fine, the maximum allowed, would have a minor impact on the company, which made $7.84 billion in profit last year.

The fine came after a U.S. review of deals Exxon signed with Rosneft, Russia's largest oil producer, weeks after Washington imposed sanctions on Moscow for annexing Ukraine's Crimea region.

Between May 14 and May 23, 2014, top U.S.-based Exxon executives signed eight documents with Igor Sechin, the head of state-run Rosneft, the Treasury's Office of Foreign Assets Control (OFAC) said in the statement on its website.

OFAC said Exxon had "demonstrated reckless disregard for U.S. sanctions requirements" by signing the deals with Sechin just weeks after the United States blacklisted him, OFAC said in the three-page statement. (For the statement, see: http://bit.ly/2vnvQf2)

The Treasury imposed sanctions on Sechin in April 2014 as part of measures to pressure Russia over its intervention in Ukraine, saying Sechin had shown "utter loyalty" to Russian President Vladimir Putin.

The sanctions prohibit U.S. citizens or people in the United States from dealing with those on the blacklist, such as Sechin. Rosneft itself is subject to narrower U.S. sanctions that still allow Americans to deal with the company on some transactions.

Exxon said in a statement that OFAC's action was "fundamentally unfair," and sued the U.S. government in Texas in an effort to overturn the decision. The company is based in Irving, Texas.

In its 21-page complaint, Exxon argued that Sechin "was subject to sanctions only in his individual capacity" and that guidance from the Obama administration at the time made clear that the sanctions "applied only to the 'personal assets' of the sanctioned individuals and emphasized that the sanctions did not restrict business with the companies those individuals managed."

(For Exxon's complaint, see: http://exxonmobil.co/2uNRWdr)

TILLERSON NOT CONSULTED

Tillerson left Exxon late last year to become secretary of state after 10 years running the company. He is now responsible for U.S. foreign policy, which includes helping make sanctions decisions.

The State Department referred questions about the fine to Exxon and the Treasury. State Department spokeswoman Heather Nauert told reporters on Thursday that the agency was alerted to the fine on Wednesday.

A Treasury spokesman said OFAC engaged with Exxon's lawyers only, and "did not discuss this case with Secretary Tillerson."

Tillerson said in January that he would recuse himself from matters involving Exxon for one year after his December 2016 resignation, unless he is authorized to participate.

Though the State Department plays a major part in formulating sanctions policy, former U.S. officials and sanctions experts said it was unlikely the agency had a role in deciding the fine announced on Thursday, because it falls under OFAC's regulatory role.

The back-and-forth between the Treasury and Exxon over the 2014 dealings spanned both the Obama and Trump administrations, and started with a subpoena from OFAC to Exxon in July 2014, Exxon said in its complaint.

Exxon fully complied with guidance from Democratic former President Barack Obama's administration that ongoing oil and gas business activities with Rosneft were permitted, Exxon spokesman Alan Jeffers said in a statement.

The Treasury "is trying to retroactively enforce a new interpretation of an executive order" inconsistent with its prior guidance, Jeffers said. "OFAC's action is fundamentally unfair."

Exxon also cited a Treasury Department representative's comments in May 2014 that BP Plc Chief Executive Bob Dudley - an American citizen - could continue to participate in Rosneft board meetings so long as they related only to Rosneft's business.

In its statement explaining the fine, OFAC said that the Treasury Department representative's comments did not address Exxon's conduct. BP did not immediately respond to a request for comment.

Publicly available guidance on the Treasury's website at the time of Exxon's dealings with Sechin said Americans should ensure they do not enter into contracts signed by sanctioned individuals, OFAC said.

And by dealing with Sechin, the company "caused significant harm" to U.S. sanctions on Russia, the agency said.

Because Rosneft itself is not off-limits to Americans, another company executive could have signed the contract with no sanctions risk to Exxon, said David Mortlock, who was a State Department and White House sanctions official under Obama.

"You could have Sechin standing over the guy's shoulder," said Mortlock, now an attorney at Willkie Farr & Gallagher LLP in Washington. "But the problem here is that it was signed by Sechin himself."

Exxon said that approach would have flown in the face of standard business practice.

"You don't ask your business partner to have someone else sign instead of the CEO," said Exxon spokesman Jeffers.

OPPOSITION TO SANCTIONS

Exxon has long opposed U.S. sanctions on Russia, saying they harm American business interests and actually help European rivals.

Tillerson said in 2014 that the company did not support sanctions because they are not effective "unless they are very well implemented."

Sanctions were a contentious topic at Tillerson's confirmation hearing last January. At the time, Republican and Democratic lawmakers were concerned that Trump, whose associates are now under investigation for their ties to Russia, would try to quickly lift U.S. sanctions on the country.

"When sanctions are imposed, they by their design are going to harm American business," Tillerson said during the hearing, in response to a question about his views on them.

He also said that Exxon "never directly lobbied against sanctions," a claim that was immediately challenged by senators who cited Exxon's own lobbying disclosure forms.

The case is Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Steve Munchin, et al, U.S. District Court, North District of Texas, No. 3:17-cv-1930.

FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson - Reuters (German)

{{20170720T210812.729+0000}}FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson(neu: Exxon klagt, Stellungnahme Finanzministerium, Kontext)

* US-Regierung verhängt Strafe wegen Sanktionsverstößen

* Geschäfte wurden 2014 unter heutigem Außenminister getätigt

* Exxon wehrt sich juristisch gegen die Entscheidung - "Unfair"

Washington/Houston, 20. Jul (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil ist wegen Russland-Geschäften zu Zeiten von US-Außenminister Rex Tillerson als Chef des Ölmultis ins Visier der heimischen Behörden geraten. Das US-Finanzministerium verhängte eine Strafe von zwei Millionen Dollar wegen Sanktionsverstößen vor gut drei Jahren. Exxon habe damals die Vorschriften "rücksichtlos missachtet", erklärte das Ministerium am Donnerstag in einer ungewöhnlich ausführlichen Stellungnahme. Konkret wird Exxon vorgeworfen, dass führende Manager im Mai 2014 Vereinbarungen über Öl- und Gasprojekte zusammen mit dem Präsidenten des russischen Konkurrenten Rosneft, Igor Setschin, unterzeichneten - wenige Wochen, nachdem die USA wegen des Ukraine-Konflikts Sanktionen gegen Russland verhängt hatten.

Die US-Regierung hatte Setschin damals wegen seiner engen Verbindung zum russischen Präsidenten Wladimir Putin auf eine schwarzen Liste gesetzt. Die Sanktionen verbieten es in den USA Ansässigen, Geschäfte mit Personen auf dieser Liste zu tätigen. Die nun verhängte Strafe resultiert aus einer Untersuchung jener Vereinbarungen, die Exxon-Manager damals mit Setschin getroffen hatten. Exxon geht juristisch gegen die Strafe vor und bezeichnete die Entscheidung als "grundlegend unfair".

Tillerson hatte Exxon zehn Jahre lang geleitet, bevor er unter US-Präsident Donald Trump zum Außenminister ernannt wurde. In dieser Position ist er mit dafür zuständig, Entscheidungen über Sanktionen zu treffen. Er gilt als russlandfreundlich und hat wiederholt die gegen das Land verhängten Strafmaßnahmen kritisiert. Daran war auch ein Plan für ein Exxon-Rosneft-Gemeinschaftsunternehmen gescheitert. Rosneft-Chef Setschin bezeichnete Tillerson einmal als Freund, mit dem er gerne mal die Vereinigten Staaten auf dem Motorrad durchqueren wolle.[nL5N1E74LZ]

(Reporter: Yeganeh Torbati und Ernest Scheyder; geschrieben von Elke Ahlswede; redigiert von Birgit Mittwollen; Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1236 oder 030-2888 5168) ((elke.ahlswede@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1732; Reuters Messaging: Elke.Ahlswede.reuters.com@reuters.net www.reuters.de www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

EEUU dice que Exxon violó sanciones a Rusia en 2014, cuando Tillerson era su presidente ejecutivo - Reuters (Spanish)

{{20170720T200520.805+0000}}EEUU dice que Exxon violó sanciones a Rusia en 2014, cuando Tillerson era su presidente ejecutivoPor Yeganeh Torbati y Ernest Scheyder

WASHINGTON/HOUSTON, 20 jul (Reuters) - Estados Unidos reprendió el jueves a Exxon Mobil Corp por su "desacato temerario" de las sanciones impuestas a los negocios con Rusia en 2014, cuando el actual secretario de Estado, Rex Tillerson, era el presidente ejecutivo de la firma, y la multó con 2 millones de dólares.

ExxonMobil dijo que la decisión fue "fundamentalmente injusta" y demandó al gobierno en Texas con el objetivo de revertirla.

La multa fue impuesta tras una revisión de los acuerdos firmados por Exxon con el principal productor petrolero ruso, Rosneft , semanas después de que Washington impusiera sanciones a Moscú por la anexión de la región ucraniana de Crimea.

Entre el 14 y el 24 de mayo de 2014, altos ejecutivos de ExxonMobil rubricaron ocho documentos con Igor Sechin, presidente de la estatal Rosneft, aseguró la Oficina de Control de Activos Extranjeros del Departamento del Tesoro (OFAC, por sus siglas en inglés) en un comunicado en su sitio web.

ExxonMobil "demostró un desacato temerario de los requisitos incluidos en las sanciones estadounidenses" al firmar acuerdos con Sechin semanas después de que Washington lo incluyera en una lista negra, indicó la OFAC en un comunicado inusualmente largo de tres páginas con sus razonamientos.

El Tesoro anunció las sanciones en abril de 2014, como parte de las medidas aprobadas para presionar a Rusia por su intervención en Ucrania, asegurando que Sechin mostró una "lealtad absoluta" al presidente ruso, Vladimir Putin.

Tillerson abandonó ExxonMobil para convertirse en secretario de Estado tras 10 años al frente de la petrolera. Ahora es el responsable de la política exterior de Estados Unidos, un cargo que incluye colaborar en las decisiones sobre sanciones.

El monto de la multa es muy pequeño para ExxonMobil, que tuvo ganancias por 7.840 millones de dólares en 2016.

(Editado en español por Carlos Serrano) ((+1-202-898-8300; Mesa de edición en español; +56224374408; Twitter: @ReutersLatam; facebook.com/ReutersLatam/)) ((REUTERS CS JL/))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

LEAD 1-Exxon à l'amende pour avoir contourné les sanctions contre Moscou - Reuters (French)

{{20170720T192746.646+0000}}LEAD 1-Exxon à l'amende pour avoir contourné les sanctions contre Moscou(Actualisé avec réaction Exxon)

WASHINGTON, 20 juillet (Reuters) - Le département du Trésor américain a condamné jeudi la société ExxonMobil et ses filiales américaines à payer une amende de deux millions de dollars (1,7 million d'euros) pour avoir contourné les sanctions contre la Russie, liées à son soutien aux rebelles ukrainiens, en mai 2014.

Le Bureau du contrôle des avoirs étrangers (OFAC) indique que la société ExxonMobil n'a pas révélé elle-même avoir transgressé les sanctions et estime qu'il s'agit d'une infraction flagrante.

ExxonMobil a dénoncé une décision "fondamentalement injuste" et déposé un recours contre le gouvernement de l'Etat du Texas dans l'espoir d'annuler la sanction.

Entre les 14 et 23 mai 2014, des dirigeants d'Exxon ont signé huit documents en lien avec des projets pétrolier et gazier en Russie avec Igor Setchine, le président de Rosneft OAO, dont les biens et les intérêts étaient bloqués par des sanctions américaines, a indiqué le Trésor américain.

Le porte-parole d'exxon, Alan Jeffers, a déclaré que l'administration Obama n'interdisait pas à l'époque de conclure des contrats avec Rosneft et Igor Setchine a signé les documents au nom de Rosneft, a-t-il souligné.

Le groupe pétrolier était alors dirigé par l'actuel secrétaire d'Etat américain, Rex Tillerson.

(Susan Heavey et Mohammed Zargham, Arthur Connan pour le service français, édité par Jean-Stéphane Brosse) ((Arthur.Connan@thomsonreuters.com; Service Informations générales 0149495334;))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

WDHLG-FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson - Reuters (German)

{{20170721T043203.671+0000}}WDHLG-FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson(Wiederholung vom Vorabend)

* US-Regierung verhängt Strafe wegen Sanktionsverstößen

* Geschäfte wurden 2014 unter heutigem Außenminister getätigt

* Exxon wehrt sich juristisch gegen die Entscheidung - "Unfair"

Washington/Houston, 20. Jul (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil ist wegen Russland-Geschäften zu Zeiten von US-Außenminister Rex Tillerson als Chef des Ölmultis ins Visier der heimischen Behörden geraten. Das US-Finanzministerium verhängte eine Strafe von zwei Millionen Dollar wegen Sanktionsverstößen vor gut drei Jahren. Exxon habe damals die Vorschriften "rücksichtlos missachtet", erklärte das Ministerium am Donnerstag in einer ungewöhnlich ausführlichen Stellungnahme. Konkret wird Exxon vorgeworfen, dass führende Manager im Mai 2014 Vereinbarungen über Öl- und Gasprojekte zusammen mit dem Präsidenten des russischen Konkurrenten Rosneft, Igor Setschin, unterzeichneten - wenige Wochen, nachdem die USA wegen des Ukraine-Konflikts Sanktionen gegen Russland verhängt hatten.

Die US-Regierung hatte Setschin damals wegen seiner engen Verbindung zum russischen Präsidenten Wladimir Putin auf eine schwarzen Liste gesetzt. Die Sanktionen verbieten es in den USA Ansässigen, Geschäfte mit Personen auf dieser Liste zu tätigen. Die nun verhängte Strafe resultiert aus einer Untersuchung jener Vereinbarungen, die Exxon-Manager damals mit Setschin getroffen hatten. Exxon geht juristisch gegen die Strafe vor und bezeichnete die Entscheidung als "grundlegend unfair".

Tillerson hatte Exxon zehn Jahre lang geleitet, bevor er unter US-Präsident Donald Trump zum Außenminister ernannt wurde. In dieser Position ist er mit dafür zuständig, Entscheidungen über Sanktionen zu treffen. Er gilt als russlandfreundlich und hat wiederholt die gegen das Land verhängten Strafmaßnahmen kritisiert. Daran war auch ein Plan für ein Exxon-Rosneft-Gemeinschaftsunternehmen gescheitert. Rosneft-Chef Setschin bezeichnete Tillerson einmal als Freund, mit dem er gerne mal die Vereinigten Staaten auf dem Motorrad durchqueren wolle.[nL5N1E74LZ]

(Reporter: Yeganeh Torbati und Ernest Scheyder; geschrieben von Elke Ahlswede; redigiert von Birgit Mittwollen; Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1236 oder 030-2888 5168) ((elke.ahlswede@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1732; Reuters Messaging: Elke.Ahlswede.reuters.com@reuters.net www.reuters.de www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

PRESS DIGEST- Wall Street Journal - July 21 - 路透新闻

{{20170721T041900.543+0000}}PRESS DIGEST- Wall Street Journal - July 21July 21 (Reuters) - The following are the top stories in the Wall Street Journal. Reuters has not verified these stories and does not vouch for their accuracy.

- The U.S. Treasury Department on Thursday imposed a $2 million fine on Exxon Mobil Corp for what it called a "reckless disregard" of U.S. sanctions on Russia while Secretary of State Rex Tillerson was the oil giant's chief executive, a finding the company immediately said it would challenge. http://on.wsj.com/2uFgiFZ

- Special Counsel Robert Mueller is investigating possible money laundering by Paul Manafort, Trump's former campaign manager, as part of his probe into what intelligence agencies say was a Kremlin-backed campaign to meddle in the election. http://on.wsj.com/2uFgFjP

- Sears Holdings Corp said Thursday it will start selling its Kenmore appliances on Amazon , loosening its grip on one of its historic product lines and becoming the latest big American brand to capitulate to the online-retail giant. http://on.wsj.com/2uEXKFK

- Blackstone recently made a roughly $3 billion bid to buy RLJ Lodging Trust , a move that if successful would end RLJ's agreement to acquire rival hotel investor FelCor Lodging Trust . RLJ said in a securities filing Monday it had rejected a $24-a-share offer from an unnamed equity firm. It isn't clear if Blackstone intends to make another offer. http://on.wsj.com/2uF6Rq7

- Billionaire entrepreneur Elon Musk, known for his teasing tweets and ever-expanding list of high-tech ambitions, set observers abuzz again with a vague claim he received "verbal" approval for a high-speed, tunnel-based travel system along one of the busiest corridors in the U.S. http://on.wsj.com/2uFgJ35

- Financier Anthony Scaramucci, a top donor to President Donald Trump during the campaign, is expected to be named White House communications director on Friday, two White House officials said. http://on.wsj.com/2uF0OBM ​

ПОВТОР-Минфин США оштрафовал Exxon Mobil на $2 млн за дела с Сечиным - Reuters (Russian)

{{20170721T040001.550+0000}}ПОВТОР-Минфин США оштрафовал Exxon Mobil на $2 млн за дела с СечинымВАШИНГТОН, 20 июл (Рейтер) - Министерство финансов США в четверг оштрафовало американский нефтяной концерн Exxon Mobil Corp и несколько его "дочек" на $2 миллиона за нарушение в мае 2014 года санкций против Игоря Сечина - главы крупнейшей нефтяной компании России Роснефть .

Пресс-секретарь Роснефти Михаил Леонтьев сказал, что не видит связи между этим событием и дальнейшим сотрудничеством Роснефти с Exxon.

Управление по контролю за иностранными активами Минфина США обнаружило, что Exxon Mobil добровольно не сообщила о нарушениях, и пришло к выводу, что "эти нарушения представляют собой вопиющий случай", говорится в сообщении, опубликованном на сайте ведомства (http://bit.ly/2vnvQf2).

Главы американских "дочек" нефтяного гиганта имели дело с теми, "чья собственность и имущественные интересы были заблокированы, в частности, подписав восемь юридических документов, связанных с нефтегазовыми проектами в России, с Игорем Сечиным, главой ОАО Роснефть" и еще одним лицом, попавшим под санкции, сообщил Минфин США.

Роснефть говорит, что американский регулятор не мог не знать о подписании документов в 2014 году.

"Три года документы находились в абсолютном доступе, и мы исключаем возможность, что OFAC про это не знал. Зная, как Exxon работает во всех вопросах с американскими санкциями, мы исключаем возможность, что Exxon не получил исчерпывающих для него разъяснений, пояснений и разрешенй от этого американского регулятора и его санкционных юристов", - сказал Леонтьев по телефону Рейтер.

UPDATE 3-Exxon sues U.S. over fine levied for Russia deal under Tillerson - Reuters News

{{20170720T230108.805+0000}}UPDATE 3-Exxon sues U.S. over fine levied for Russia deal under Tillerson(Recasts, adds material from lawsuit)

By Yeganeh Torbati and Ernest Scheyder

WASHINGTON/HOUSTON, July 20 (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil Corp sued the U.S. government on Thursday, blasting as "unlawful" and "capricious" a $2 million fine levied against it for a three-year-old oil joint venture with Russia's Rosneft .

The U.S. Treasury Department on Thursday morning slapped the world's largest publicly traded oil producer with the fine for "reckless disregard" of U.S. sanctions in dealings with Russia in 2014 when Secretary of State Rex Tillerson was Exxon's chief executive.

The lawsuit and the Treasury's unusually detailed statement on Exxon's conduct represented an extraordinary confrontation between a major American company and the U.S. government, made all the more striking because Exxon's former CEO is now in President Donald Trump's Cabinet.

Exxon took the government to court despite the fact that the fine, the maximum allowed, would have a minor impact on the company, which made $7.84 billion in profit last year.

The fine came after a U.S. review of deals Exxon signed with Rosneft, Russia's largest oil producer, weeks after Washington imposed sanctions on Moscow for annexing Ukraine's Crimea region.

Between May 14 and May 23, 2014, top U.S.-based Exxon executives signed eight documents with Igor Sechin, the head of state-run Rosneft, the Treasury's Office of Foreign Assets Control (OFAC) said in the statement on its website.

OFAC said Exxon had "demonstrated reckless disregard for U.S. sanctions requirements" by signing the deals with Sechin just weeks after the United States blacklisted him, OFAC said in the three-page statement. (For the statement, see: http://bit.ly/2vnvQf2)

The Treasury imposed sanctions on Sechin in April 2014 as part of measures to pressure Russia over its intervention in Ukraine, saying Sechin had shown "utter loyalty" to Russian President Vladimir Putin.

The sanctions prohibit U.S. citizens or people in the United States from dealing with those on the blacklist, such as Sechin. Rosneft itself is subject to narrower U.S. sanctions that still allow Americans to deal with the company on some transactions.

Exxon said in a statement that OFAC's action was "fundamentally unfair," and sued the U.S. government in Texas in an effort to overturn the decision. The company is based in Irving, Texas.

In its 21-page complaint, Exxon argued that Sechin "was subject to sanctions only in his individual capacity" and that guidance from the Obama administration at the time made clear that the sanctions "applied only to the 'personal assets' of the sanctioned individuals and emphasized that the sanctions did not restrict business with the companies those individuals managed."

(For Exxon's complaint, see: http://exxonmobil.co/2uNRWdr)

TILLERSON NOT CONSULTED

Tillerson left Exxon late last year to become secretary of state after 10 years running the company. He is now responsible for U.S. foreign policy, which includes helping make sanctions decisions.

The State Department referred questions about the fine to Exxon and the Treasury. State Department spokeswoman Heather Nauert told reporters on Thursday that the agency was alerted to the fine on Wednesday.

A Treasury spokesman said OFAC engaged with Exxon's lawyers only, and "did not discuss this case with Secretary Tillerson."

Tillerson said in January that he would recuse himself from matters involving Exxon for one year after his December 2016 resignation, unless he is authorized to participate.

Though the State Department plays a major part in formulating sanctions policy, former U.S. officials and sanctions experts said it was unlikely the agency had a role in deciding the fine announced on Thursday, because it falls under OFAC's regulatory role.

The back-and-forth between the Treasury and Exxon over the 2014 dealings spanned both the Obama and Trump administrations, and started with a subpoena from OFAC to Exxon in July 2014, Exxon said in its complaint.

Exxon fully complied with guidance from Democratic former President Barack Obama's administration that ongoing oil and gas business activities with Rosneft were permitted, Exxon spokesman Alan Jeffers said in a statement.

The Treasury "is trying to retroactively enforce a new interpretation of an executive order" inconsistent with its prior guidance, Jeffers said. "OFAC's action is fundamentally unfair."

Exxon also cited a Treasury Department representative's comments in May 2014 that BP Plc Chief Executive Bob Dudley - an American citizen - could continue to participate in Rosneft board meetings so long as they related only to Rosneft's business.

In its statement explaining the fine, OFAC said that the Treasury Department representative's comments did not address Exxon's conduct. BP did not immediately respond to a request for comment.

Publicly available guidance on the Treasury's website at the time of Exxon's dealings with Sechin said Americans should ensure they do not enter into contracts signed by sanctioned individuals, OFAC said.

And by dealing with Sechin, the company "caused significant harm" to U.S. sanctions on Russia, the agency said.

Because Rosneft itself is not off-limits to Americans, another company executive could have signed the contract with no sanctions risk to Exxon, said David Mortlock, who was a State Department and White House sanctions official under Obama.

"You could have Sechin standing over the guy's shoulder," said Mortlock, now an attorney at Willkie Farr & Gallagher LLP in Washington. "But the problem here is that it was signed by Sechin himself."

Exxon said that approach would have flown in the face of standard business practice.

"You don't ask your business partner to have someone else sign instead of the CEO," said Exxon spokesman Jeffers.

OPPOSITION TO SANCTIONS

Exxon has long opposed U.S. sanctions on Russia, saying they harm American business interests and actually help European rivals.

Tillerson said in 2014 that the company did not support sanctions because they are not effective "unless they are very well implemented."

Sanctions were a contentious topic at Tillerson's confirmation hearing last January. At the time, Republican and Democratic lawmakers were concerned that Trump, whose associates are now under investigation for their ties to Russia, would try to quickly lift U.S. sanctions on the country.

"When sanctions are imposed, they by their design are going to harm American business," Tillerson said during the hearing, in response to a question about his views on them.

He also said that Exxon "never directly lobbied against sanctions," a claim that was immediately challenged by senators who cited Exxon's own lobbying disclosure forms.

The case is Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Steve Munchin, et al, U.S. District Court, North District of Texas, No. 3:17-cv-1930.

FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson - Reuters (German)

{{20170720T210812.729+0000}}FOKUS 1-Strafe gegen Exxon wegen Russland-Deals unter Tillerson(neu: Exxon klagt, Stellungnahme Finanzministerium, Kontext)

* US-Regierung verhängt Strafe wegen Sanktionsverstößen

* Geschäfte wurden 2014 unter heutigem Außenminister getätigt

* Exxon wehrt sich juristisch gegen die Entscheidung - "Unfair"

Washington/Houston, 20. Jul (Reuters) - Exxon Mobil ist wegen Russland-Geschäften zu Zeiten von US-Außenminister Rex Tillerson als Chef des Ölmultis ins Visier der heimischen Behörden geraten. Das US-Finanzministerium verhängte eine Strafe von zwei Millionen Dollar wegen Sanktionsverstößen vor gut drei Jahren. Exxon habe damals die Vorschriften "rücksichtlos missachtet", erklärte das Ministerium am Donnerstag in einer ungewöhnlich ausführlichen Stellungnahme. Konkret wird Exxon vorgeworfen, dass führende Manager im Mai 2014 Vereinbarungen über Öl- und Gasprojekte zusammen mit dem Präsidenten des russischen Konkurrenten Rosneft, Igor Setschin, unterzeichneten - wenige Wochen, nachdem die USA wegen des Ukraine-Konflikts Sanktionen gegen Russland verhängt hatten.

Die US-Regierung hatte Setschin damals wegen seiner engen Verbindung zum russischen Präsidenten Wladimir Putin auf eine schwarzen Liste gesetzt. Die Sanktionen verbieten es in den USA Ansässigen, Geschäfte mit Personen auf dieser Liste zu tätigen. Die nun verhängte Strafe resultiert aus einer Untersuchung jener Vereinbarungen, die Exxon-Manager damals mit Setschin getroffen hatten. Exxon geht juristisch gegen die Strafe vor und bezeichnete die Entscheidung als "grundlegend unfair".

Tillerson hatte Exxon zehn Jahre lang geleitet, bevor er unter US-Präsident Donald Trump zum Außenminister ernannt wurde. In dieser Position ist er mit dafür zuständig, Entscheidungen über Sanktionen zu treffen. Er gilt als russlandfreundlich und hat wiederholt die gegen das Land verhängten Strafmaßnahmen kritisiert. Daran war auch ein Plan für ein Exxon-Rosneft-Gemeinschaftsunternehmen gescheitert. Rosneft-Chef Setschin bezeichnete Tillerson einmal als Freund, mit dem er gerne mal die Vereinigten Staaten auf dem Motorrad durchqueren wolle.[nL5N1E74LZ]

(Reporter: Yeganeh Torbati und Ernest Scheyder; geschrieben von Elke Ahlswede; redigiert von Birgit Mittwollen; Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1236 oder 030-2888 5168) ((elke.ahlswede@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1732; Reuters Messaging: Elke.Ahlswede.reuters.com@reuters.net www.reuters.de www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters
